## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting mechanical stress (sigma) from strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a classic problem in materials science and solid mechanics. The relationship captures how materials deform under load and how temperature affects mechanical properties such as elastic modulus, yield strength, and flow stress.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': "Hooke's law (linear elastic)", 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon', 'scenario': 'Linear elastic regime, small strains'}
- {'name': "Temperature-dependent Hooke's law", 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent elastic modulus'}
- {'name': 'Power-law hardening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1', 'scenario': 'Strain hardening in plastic deformation (Hollomon equation)'}
- {'name': 'Ramberg-Osgood type', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2', 'scenario': 'Combined elastic and plastic deformation'}
- {'name': 'Temperature-dependent power-law hardening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'Strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Johnson-Cook type (simplified)', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)', 'scenario': 'Flow stress with strain hardening and linear thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Thermal softening with power-law temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T**c2)', 'scenario': 'Elastic modulus degradation with temperature'}
- {'name': 'Exponential thermal softening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T)', 'scenario': 'Exponential decrease of stiffness with temperature'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial stress-strain', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3', 'scenario': 'Nonlinear elastic or hyperelastic material behavior'}
- {'name': 'Temperature-dependent polynomial', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2', 'scenario': 'Nonlinear stress-strain with temperature-dependent coefficients'}
- {'name': 'Voce hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon))', 'scenario': 'Saturating stress with exponential approach to steady state'}
- {'name': 'Temperature-dependent Voce', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))', 'scenario': 'Saturating hardening with thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Ludwik equation', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2', 'scenario': 'Yield stress plus power-law hardening'}
- {'name': 'Inverse temperature modulus', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * T)', 'scenario': 'Rational thermal softening of elastic modulus'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T^n) or exp(-c*T) on stress terms
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic stress plateau
- Power-law plasticity → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 indicates work hardening with diminishing returns
- Separable temperature-strain coupling → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) where f captures hardening and g captures thermal softening
- Yield offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield stress before hardening contribution
- Polynomial nonlinear elasticity → Odd powers of epsilon (epsilon, epsilon^3) for symmetric tension-compression behavior
- Competing thermal mechanisms → Sum of Arrhenius terms exp(c1/T) + exp(c2/T) for diffusion-controlled deformation
- Strain-temperature cross term → epsilon*T product indicating thermomechanical coupling effects

Let me expand the first term:
```
61.35*epsilon*(-0.05077*T + 0.05077*278.15 + 1) = 61.35*epsilon*(-0.05077*T + 15.12)
```

So GT has three main components:
1. **Linear in epsilon, linear in T**: `61.35*epsilon*(-0.05077*T + 15.12)` = terms with `epsilon*T` and `epsilon`
2. **Fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius**: `98.58*epsilon^0.3178*exp(-49.46/(8.314*T))` = `epsilon^0.3178 * exp(-c/T)`
3. **Power of epsilon times linear in T**: `2.304*epsilon^1.450*(T - 278.15)` = terms with `epsilon^1.450*T` and `epsilon^1.450`

The key basis functions are:
- `epsilon` (linear)
- `epsilon * T` (interaction)
- `epsilon^0.3178 * exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius-type)
- `epsilon^1.450` (fractional power)
- `epsilon^1.450 * T` (fractional power times T)

Let me now check each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether each candidate can reproduce these basis functions.

The critical distinguishing features are:
- The Arrhenius term `exp(-c/T)` (or equivalently `exp(c/T)`)
- The `epsilon*T` cross-term
- The `epsilon^c * T` cross-term

**Candidate 1:** `(T*c0 + c1 + (c2*tanh(c3*epsilon + c4) + c5*epsilon^(1/3)*exp(c6*epsilon))*(c7*epsilon + c8))/(c7*epsilon + c8)`

This has `tanh`, `exp(c*epsilon)`, and a rational function of epsilon with T. Cannot match Arrhenius `exp(-c/T)`. The T dependence is wrong - it appears as `T/(c7*epsilon+c8)` not as `epsilon*T`.

**Candidate 35:** Let me expand:
`(c0*epsilon*(c1 + epsilon) + (T*c2 + 1)*(c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon^(1/3)*(c1 + epsilon)*(T*c5 + 1)))/((c1 + epsilon)*(T*c2 + 1))`

Wait, let me redo this more carefully:
Numerator: `c0*epsilon*(c1+epsilon) + (T*c2+1)*(c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon^(1/3)*(c1+epsilon)*(T*c5+1))`
Denominator: `(c1+epsilon)*(T*c2+1)`

= `c0*epsilon*(c1+epsilon)/((c1+epsilon)*(T*c2+1)) + (T*c2+1)*c3*epsilon/((c1+epsilon)*(T*c2+1)) + (T*c2+1)*c4*epsilon^(1/3)*(c1+epsilon)*(T*c5+1)/((c1+epsilon)*(T*c2+1))`
